Could the shaking when not constantly eating be caused by gestational diabetes? Gestational diabetes is when a mother becomes diabetic when pregnant. According to the CDC, there usually aren't any symptoms of gestational diabetes, but this may be a good starting place. I would explain to your doctor your symptoms and ask to be tested for gestational diabstes. I hope this helps. Here is a link to the CDC article I skimmed through about gestational diabetes: https://www.cdc.gov

Typically twins (or multiples) are born via c-section because if one baby is born head first, the second baby may present in a different position (butt first, back first, feet first) which then makes it dangerous for the second baby. A lot of doctors prefer to go the safest route (c-section) but some doctors will work with you to ensure that you can deliver both vaginally.

I am slightly anemic tho, so I understand the bloodsugar and low-iron shakes very well. Bagel, pop tarts and grapes = NOT blood sugar stabilizing = shaky and energy crashes. Your insulin/blood sugar needs to be stable throughout the day to keep you from getting shaky and hangry. Starting the day with protein is super important! Sets you up for more stable blood sugar even if you eat the pop tarts later. That being said, I know it's hard when you feel sick amd you crave comfort foods and carbs,  but I would suggest finding a way to eat something like eggs, meat, yogurt (low sugar), nuts...something high in protein and then try eating the carbs. Your blood sugar will thank youğŸ’•
It doesnâ€™t matter so much the amount of food you eat, but the amount of energy your body is able to get from that food.   *TW Iâ€™m going to mention specific foods, gag at your own risk*   I.e. if you were to eat a whole bunch of cookies, letâ€™s say your body would be able to use 40% of each cookie as fuel to help power your cells and grow your babies. If you were to eat a sweet potato letâ€™s say your body would be able to use 70% of a sweet potato as fuel. In order to get the same amount of fuel/energy from cookies as you would from a sweet potato, you would need to eat more cookies. Because the cookies are a simpler carbohydrate you would need to eat again much sooner to maintain the glucose that your cells are using. A more complex carbohydrate may last your closer to 3 hours.     It sounds like you might be experiencing low blood sugar. From the foods youâ€™ve listed youâ€™re consuming a lot of â€œsimpleâ€ carbs. This is not a bad thing, it just means your body can put that fuel to use easier and faster than other carbs. Low blood glucose makes me either very nauseous and confused or ravenous and dazed. Either way Iâ€™m a little foggy lol. Your body tells you it needs more fuel ASAP when your blood glucose levels are reduced and your instinct will be to have more simple sugars because they get the job done quick. This is all further complicated by your inability to tolerate the idea of most foods due to your pregnancy. When possible, it would help to combine your simple carbs with something fibrous or to swap for a more complex carb.

Bagels, pop tarts and grapes are all quick-release carbs that don't keep you full for very long, even if you're not pregnant. I think the shakes are from hypoglycaemia (=low blood sugar) that follows after a sugar spike is over. To prevent the shakes, try eating some protein and fats with every snack / meal. Proteins and fats help keep you full for longer.

FOR NAUSEA!! There is something similar to those generic nausea wristbands, but it's electronic. It's called the EmeTerm wristband, or another brand is ReliefBand (looks nicer and has more setting options, but the battery life is crummy). It's like a weak miniature TENS unit, it sends tiny electric pulses to the same nerve that the basic elastic/button wristbands hit. It is completely safe for pregnant women, a lot of doctors even recommend it! I have only used it for nausea from other things, not pregnancy, but I know quite a few pregnant women who loved it!! They're not the cheapest thing in the world (usually around $120, but their website has them on sale right now), but they have a great return policy if it doesn't work for you. They also last for years. I've had mine for 3 years now, and it's still going strong!  Edited to add: It uses the same nerves on your wrist as the cheap "elastic band with a plastic button" things, but it does actually work in a different way, it's not just a more expensive version of the same thing. So one might work when the other doesn't.

Colleen, I am one of three identical triplet girls. Our parents thought they were having boys (in 1958 they didn't have today's technology). They didn't even think of girls names!! It took them 3 days to decide and then they said to heck with middle names. We each got only the initial for the order we were born in! I was born 3rd so my middle name is just the initial "C". When you talked about your twins being Baby A and Baby B, it made me think of us. We were so blessed, my mother carried us to full term and delivered us naturally on December 9th, which was also our dad's birthday. We were all 6-7 lbs and perfectly healthy. And the next day we were on the front page of the San Diego newspaper with our dad, because triplets were rare then.  P.S. They already had THREE children!

Hey Colleen! While I think you are 1000% right about being thankful that companies are participating in pride and grateful that the world is slowly becoming more accepting, I think the actual reason people are hating on the looks of the clothes is that they feel as if it was slapped together quickly for pride month. As in, these companies are just sticking rainbows on clothes and calling them pride clothing in order to gain money. Yet for the other 11 months of the year, they do nothing to support lgbtq+ people, and many are even outwardly homophobic the rest of the year. The problem is that these places are using pride for their own gain and not because they actually care. And since lgtbq+ people can't stop these businesses from using the lgbtq+ identities for their own gain and corporate greed, pointing out the looks of the clothes is to discourage people to not buy it and point out how the companies don't actually care enough about pride to put effort into their designs.

Not to scare you (like Colleen is going to read this, but it's my two cents, and what it's worth LOL), but the first c-section, in my opinion, is harder than subsequent ones.  Mine was called a "classical" which means from the bottom of my belly button to the top of my pubic bone down the middle.  It's usually only done in an emergency, which was what mine was... problem is, once you've had a "classical" c-section, I think you are always going to have to have one.  Usually, the most common method now is in the bikini line and this seems to be a lot easier for women.. different muscles are cut, etc.   My first birth was a singleton but my second was twins and there was no way I was going to attempt a VBAC (vaginal birth after cesarean).   I hope you can deliver vaginally but if not, you will do fine with a section.. gotta get those babies out somehow!   I truly hope that your nausea subsides and that this pregnancy is easier than your first but with twins, it may not be.  I think state of mind goes a long way.. if you wake up thinking that it's going to be a horrible day, chances are, it will type thing.  I am going to think positively for you.   Love your vlogs, love your family and trying to be supportive.  You do you boo!!!!
Good luck with the blood test for the twins! Love you and have a good day
